Third, the M6+ strata do not extend to longer windows (all CIs cross zero; recorded unestablished) -- the established rare-event result remains the 7-day M6+ mainshock gain of round 12. The review also surfaced a structural honesty property worth recording: the realized-by-6h exclusion discards 200 thirty-day positives whose qualifying event genuinely occurs after the feature window -- early-loud sequences where the 6h features are most informative -- so the honest metric is, by construction, conservative against the model. Queued next: growing the M6+ class (catalogue extension before 2000, subject to per-year completeness), and detection-corrected productivity adaptation.

**2026-07-11 update 10 (fourteenth round: the catalogue extended to 1990 and the walk-forward doubled to ten folds -- the main lever survives its hardest test yet, and the rare-event stratum is honestly downgraded).** Ten more years of JMA hypocentre decks were added (1997 ships as two half-year files; month-coverage verified continuous), the extended cache's post-2000 portion verified multiset-identical to the reviewed catalogue, and the per-year completeness gate passed (1990s Mc 1.0-2.4, far below the M3.5 driver band). Five further ETAS fits (2002-2010 splits, all converged; parameters shift smoothly into the sparser-network training era, train-only so leak-irrelevant) yield five new test folds, making ten non-overlapping windows spanning 2002-2024 with 946 pooled forecast-only positives. Two results, in opposite directions and both worth recording. First, the main ETAS lever posts +0.047 (CI [+0.035,+0.058], P(d>0)=1.000), identical to the third decimal in the 2002-2011 and 2012-2024 eras separately and positive in all ten folds -- the strongest replication this catalogue span can offer. Second, the M6+ mainshock stratum, at 34 positives (2.4x the round-12 power), drops to +0.043 with the CI crossing zero and is downgraded to unestablished: the +0.191 (round 11) -> +0.094 (round 12) -> +0.043 shrinkage is the classic signature of small-sample optimism, and the formal era-difference test (late-minus-early +0.087, CI [-0.012,+0.189], p=0.083) says the apparent early/late gap is itself consistent with noise -- one homogeneous ~+0.04 effect, not era heterogeneity. The review attacked in both directions -- gain artifacts and dilution-as-bug -- and cleared both: the early-era positives are real events, the famous absences (Tokachi-oki 2003, Chuetsu 2004, Tohoku 2011) are the honest metric correctly excluding sequences whose escalation had already begun within the six-hour feature window, and the ETAS features are non-degenerate with era-matched distributions; every review number was independently re-run and reproduced. Where this leaves the rare-event goal: decks exist back to at least 1983, but the shrinkage pattern argues the deeper lever is methodological -- borrowing strength from the abundant sub-M6 class (hierarchical/transfer formulations) rather than only adding years. Queued: that, and detection-corrected productivity adaptation.

**2026-07-11 update 11 (fifteenth round: magnitude-weighted training for the rare-event stratum -- decisively harmful, with the mechanism identified).** The first methodological lever for the M6+ class was tested: retraining the full stack with Gutenberg-Richter-informed sample weights (10^(beta(Mm-4.5)), beta 0.5 and 1.0) to emphasise the sparse large-magnitude regime, against the unweighted reference -- whose scores were first verified bit-identical to the round-14 dumps, so the measured deltas are purely the weighting effect. The result is a clean dose-dependent harm: on the pre-registered primary metric (pooled M6+ union, 54 positives) the weighted model scores -0.052 (P(worse)=0.997) at beta=0.5 and -0.090 (CI [-0.144,-0.036]) at beta=1.0, with the M6+ mainshock stratum dropping as far as -0.136; the all-forecast-only guard degrades too at the stronger dose. The mechanism is textbook and quantified: the effective training sample collapses from 5,644 to 1,548 at beta=0.5 and to eight (the top ten events carrying 48% of total weight) at beta=1.0 -- upweighting a sparse regime discards the abundant sub-M6 signal without adding generalisable large-magnitude information. This negative resolves the within-catalogue reweighting family and reinforces the round-14 framing: the escalation signal is homogeneous across magnitude, and the M6+ class is short on statistics, not on emphasis. Remaining levers for the rare-event goal, queued: extending the catalogue to 1983 (decks confirmed to exist; the per-year completeness gate is the deciding check, as the 1980s network was sparser), and detection-corrected productivity adaptation.

**2026-07-11 update 12 (sixteenth round: the catalogue reaches 1983 and the walk-forward reaches thirteen folds -- the lever is confirmed magnitude-uniform, era-uniform, and the queued adaptation lever is closed).** Seven more deck years were added (the 1990-onward portion of the new cache verified multiset-identical to the reviewed one; the 1983 completeness sits at the M3.5 driver-band edge and is recorded as a caveat, though the MC=3.5 gate keeps sub-threshold incompleteness out of every feature), three further pre-2002 fits converged (their Omori p dips below 1 in the sparse-network era; the integral form was verified well-behaved), and three new test folds make thirteen non-overlapping windows tiling 1996-2024 exactly -- 7,195 test events, zero duplicates, 1,151 forecast-only positives. The main ETAS lever posts +0.044 (CI [+0.033,+0.055], P(d>0)=1.000), positive in all thirteen folds (sign-test p~1e-4, cluster-robust beyond the pooled bootstrap). The rare-event strata are now best summarised by the homogeneity tests: both M6+ strata are statistically indistinguishable from the single magnitude-uniform ~+0.044 effect (differences n.s. at P=0.687/0.383). The M6+ follow-up stratum does cross nominal significance (+0.055, P=0.993), but the review's decomposition -- independently re-run -- shows the crossing is carried by four sparse-era 1996-2000 positives scoring +0.200 while the 2002-2020 folds alone remain CI-crossing-zero: it is recorded as consistent with the uniform effect, not as a rare-event discovery, and the honest reading of "uniform" is "no premium larger than ~0.05 detected", not "proven equal". Separately, the long-queued adaptation lever was closed: the detection-corrected (Omi/Helmstetter) per-sequence productivity update -- whose first implementation used the wrong completeness convention and was caught inert by a mechanism audit before any conclusion -- scores -0.010 (CI [-0.018,-0.002]) against the generic forward forecast once corrected, the same null as the simple counting version, and the detection model demonstrably cannot explain the moderate-mainshock count deficit that motivated it. The verified honest state of this formulation: pooled walk-forward 0.753 (7-day window), single-split best 0.752, thirty-day window 0.796. Queued next: tectonic-context features from the Slab2 subduction geometry model (grids already staged and read-verified; 88% epicentre coverage, the open question being incremental value beyond the spatial climatology the model already holds).

**2026-07-11 update 13 (eighteenth round: Slab2 tectonic-context features -- a well-powered null).** The staged tectonic lever was executed: four static features from the USGS Slab2 subduction-geometry model (slab depth at the epicentre, the event's depth relative to the slab surface, slab dip, and a no-coverage flag -- Nankai lies outside Slab2 and enters as native missing values), computed for all thirteen sample sets at 88-90% coverage, with univariate label correlations around -0.15 suggesting real marginal structure. Added to the full stack in the same thirteen-fold walk-forward, they change nothing: -0.002 on all forecast-only positives with a tight CI [-0.006,+0.003] at 1,151 positives, and every M6+ stratum flat. The audit confirms this is a genuine null rather than a plumbing artifact -- the reference reproduces the round-16 scores bit-identically while the variant's scores differ on every test event, so the models demonstrably used the features and extracted nothing incremental: the spatial background and location/depth features already carry whatever tectonic information this target can use. The magnitude-weighting (round 15), adaptation (rounds 9/17), Coulomb (round 10), and now slab-geometry families are all resolved; the verified state stands at pooled walk-forward 0.753 (7-day), single-split 0.752, thirty-day window 0.796, with the ETAS forward-forecast/context levers the only confirmed skill source beyond the static baseline. Queued next, the largest untested axis inside this formulation: replacing the hand-crafted feature representation itself with a learned sequence model over the raw pre-history and first-six-hours event streams.

**2026-07-11 update 14 (nineteenth round: a learned sequence representation -- the blend is null, and the null is informative).** The largest untested axis inside the formulation was probed: a small two-stream GRU trained per fold on the raw event streams themselves (the first six hours inside the Gardner-Knopoff disc, and thirty days of pre-history within twice the radius), with temporal early stopping inside the training period and a fixed a-priori 50/50 rank-blend against the gradient-boosted full stack as the pre-registered primary. The blend changes nothing: +0.001 (CI [-0.006,+0.008]) on 1,151 pooled forecast-only positives, all M6+ strata flat, with the reference again verified bit-identical to the round-16 scores. The informative part is the network alone: from raw streams, with no hand-crafted features at all, it reaches pooled 0.722 -- above the 16-feature static baseline (0.709), most of the way to the full ETAS stack (0.753), and fold-competitive with it in four of thirteen windows. Two independent representation families -- hand-crafted seismological features plus ETAS model quantities, and a from-scratch learned encoder -- thus converge on the same skill band and share almost all their information, which argues the formulation is not representation-bottlenecked at this model scale (a caveat stands: a GPU-scale sequence model is a different, untested regime). The practical conclusion recorded for the arc: further gains most plausibly require new information rather than better encoding of the same catalogue streams -- with cross-region training catalogues (Southern California, Italy, and other open regional networks, used to augment training while keeping the Japan-only honest evaluation untouched) the leading queued lever.

**2026-07-11 update 15 (twentieth round: cross-region training augmentation from New Zealand -- a marginal null that sharpens the diagnosis).** The "new information" lever was executed with the nearest feature-compatible donor: the full GeoNet catalogue (106k events after box and type filtering; completeness verified below the M3.5 driver band), a New-Zealand ETAS fit on 1990-2005 only (converging to a genuinely different regime -- productivity exponent 0.96, spatial scale 14 km2 versus Japan's 0.5-0.7 and ~0.6), and the identical sequence/feature pipeline, augmenting the training set of the eight post-2006 folds while leaving the Japan-only honest evaluation untouched (no label leak is possible from a foreign region by construction; the Japan-only reference again reproduces the prior scores bit-identically). Doubling the training positives this way moves the pooled honest AUC by +0.005 (CI [-0.001,+0.011], P=0.949) -- a positive lean short of significance -- while the M6+ strata lean slightly negative (n.s.), and a region-indicator variant produces bit-identical scores because no tree ever splits on it: the model itself judges the regional distinction uninformative in this feature space. Recorded as a marginal null with honest caveats (single donor, magnitude-scale mismatch, and only ~1,800 donor rows at the late splits); the hundredfold-larger global NEIC catalogue (216k M4.5+ events, existence probed) remains the untested scale escalation of this family. Together with round 19, the diagnosis sharpens: the current feature space appears signal-saturated by the Japan catalogue alone -- the next gains must come from either genuinely new measurement channels or a structurally different target, and the arc continues on that basis.

**2026-07-11 update 16 (twenty-first round: global-scale mainshock augmentation from the worldwide NEIC catalogue -- the pre-registered rare-event target is null, and the scale-augmentation family closes).** The hundredfold escalation queued at the end of round 20 was executed: the worldwide ComCat/NEIC catalogue over 35 years (M4.5+ 193,873 events after excluding the Japan box and non-earthquake types), Gardner-Knopoff declustered into 10,745 independent mainshocks at Mm>=5.5 -- of which 3,625 are M6+, roughly seven times the Japanese count -- carried through the identical sequence and feature pipeline (the eight ETAS columns NaN-filled for global rows, the Gardner-Knopoff labels being deterministic so no per-event fit is needed and no Japan-label leak is possible by construction), then used to augment the training rows of all thirteen walk-forward folds while the Japan-only honest evaluation is left untouched. The pre-registered primary was the M6+ union delta -- the entire reason to inject seven times more large mainshocks -- and it is null to slightly negative: the M6+ follow-up stratum moves -0.009 (n.s.) and the M6+ mainshock stratum -0.029 (nominal P=0.026, but small-sample and Taiwan-driven, softening to P=0.055 with Taiwan removed), so read as no rare-event gain with a weak negative lean rather than robust harm. The pooled all-forecast AUC rises a marginal +0.006 (0.753 -> 0.759, CI [+0.001,+0.012]) -- a small generic ETAS-context uplift an order of magnitude below the confirmed ETAS lever (+0.044), reproduced bit-identically on an independent second pooling run, and not the M6+ skill sought. This closes the cross-region and scale-augmentation family (round 20's New-Zealand marginal null followed by round 21's global-scale null on the target): within the current feature space, more same-kind catalogue data -- of any regime or any volume -- saturates, exactly as round 19 argued when a from-scratch learned encoder converged on the same skill band as the hand-crafted stack. Recorded as a lever tried and found null on its target, not a ceiling: the diagnosis that the next gain must introduce information the earthquake catalogue does not carry now rests on three independent lines of evidence, and the arc continues by searching for that new channel or a structurally different target.

**2026-07-11 update 17 (twenty-second round: mainshock focal mechanism from GlobalCMT -- a well-powered null, including on the M6+ target it was built for).** With rounds 19-21 converging on "the next gain needs information the catalogue does not carry," the mainshock source geometry (faulting style) was tested as exactly such a channel -- distinct from magnitude and location and from the round-18 static Slab2 position, since a subduction-interface thrust and a crustal strike-slip of equal size can escalate differently, and the mechanism is known at forecast time (routine within hours) so no label leak is possible. The full 1996-2024 GlobalCMT catalogue was assembled with complete temporal coverage (the 1976-2020 combined file plus reviewed monthly 2021-2024 plus the quick catalogue), yielding 5,648 Japan-box solutions, and each mainshock was matched to its moment tensor by the stable catalogue index -- 92.5% of the M6+ mainshocks matched, near-complete on the rare-event stratum that matters. Seven nodal-plane-ambiguity-free focal features (the P/T/B principal-axis plunges plus the rake sine/cosine and both dips) were appended to the confirmed stack, with the reference verified bit-identical to the round-21 baseline so the delta isolates the mechanism, and the variant demonstrably enters the trees rather than being a degenerate no-op. It changes nothing: pooled all-forecast +0.000 (CI [-0.004,+0.004]), M6+ follow-up -0.001, M6+ mainshock -0.015 (n.s.), Taiwan-excluded follow-up +0.003 -- a well-powered null on every stratum, reproduced on an independent second pooling. The most plausible reading is that the model already infers the tectonic setting from location and depth, so the explicit mechanism is redundant information under a new label -- the same saturation seen when a learned encoder, a cross-region catalogue, and a global-scale catalogue each added nothing. This is now the fourth independent line pointing to the same diagnosis; recorded as a lever tried and found null on its target, not a ceiling, and the search continues for a channel carrying information that location and the catalogue genuinely lack, or for a structurally different target.

**2026-07-11 update 18 (twenty-third round: sub-Mc micro-seismicity / catalogue completeness -- the gain saturates at completeness ~1.0 and the template-matching ultra-tail is null-to-negative, a fifth independent saturation line).** With rounds 19-22 converging on "the next gain needs information the catalogue does not carry," one untested class of genuinely new information is catalogue COMPLETENESS itself: the dense sub-Mc micro-seismicity a template-matching catalogue resolves but a standard-completeness catalogue misses, concentrated in the immediate post-mainshock coda where nucleation signal would live. Japan sub-Mc coverage is registration-gated, so the clean open test was run cross-region on the Southern California QTM catalogue (Ross et al. 2019; 1.81 million events, completeness ~0.3, 2008-2017). The design is a single-catalogue, multi-completeness contrast that eliminates every cross-catalogue artefact: independent Mm>=3.0 mainshocks (Gardner-Knopoff) with an escalation label defined on events at least a magnitude unit below the mainshock (>=2.0, far above every truncation, so labels are bit-identical across variants), and strict-causal density features (first 6 h, aftershock count/rate/b-value/inter-event and spatial statistics) rebuilt three times from the SAME catalogue truncated at completeness 1.7 (standard proxy), 1.0 (this project's pipeline level) and 0.3 (full). The leak-free primary (6 h features only; kept sequences exclude escalations already realised within 6 h, machine-verified to contain zero label events inside the window) shows skill rise from 1.7 to 1.0 -- +0.031 AUC at the 7-day horizon (CI [+0.006,+0.057], P 0.99) -- then FALL from 1.0 to 0.3: the ultra-tail change is -0.026 (CI [-0.052,-0.001], P 0.02), a statistically resolved non-monotonicity rather than an underpowered null, and specific to the short horizon (at 30 days the two are indistinguishable), consistent with short-term aftershock incompleteness corrupting the sub-1.0 events in the decisive early coda. The optimum completeness is ~1.0 -- exactly the level this project's Japan pipeline already builds features at -- so deeper catalogue density is, in isolation, not a route to higher skill; the one caveat left open by adversarial review is a sub-completeness by ETAS-context interaction, which a density-only isolation cannot test. Recorded as a lever tried and found null-to-negative below completeness 1.0 on target, not a ceiling: a fifth independent line -- learned encoder, cross-region, global-scale, source geometry, and now catalogue density -- pointing to the same saturation of the location-plus-catalogue paradigm under this target, and the search continues for a channel carrying information the catalogue genuinely lacks or a structurally different target.

**2026-07-12 update 19 (twenty-fourth round: crustal-specialist, migration-conditioned escalation -- the one channel with an established real signal, and it is real-but-redundant, a sixth independent saturation line).** Five converging null lines said the next gain needs information location and the catalogue do not carry; the one arc that DID find a physically real signal is foreshock radial-migration (foreshocks contracting toward the mainshock nucleus over ~14 days, crustal-specific, with subduction megathrust statistically separating out), so the natural test was whether that signal TRANSFERS to escalation forecasting. The population was restricted to crustal mainshocks (depth <= 30 km) and six pre-mainshock migration-kinematics features were added to the confirmed stack -- the Spearman distance-versus-time trend (negative = contraction), the linear shrink rate and its R-squared, the early-half-versus-late-half centroid approach, the azimuthal concentration, and the log foreshock count -- all computed strictly before the trigger time, within a magnitude-only Gardner-Knopoff radius, and relative to the KNOWN trigger location, so the future strong-follow-up hypocentre is never used (leak-safety confirmed by adversarial review, which bit-reproduced the per-fold features from scratch). Across the 13-fold 1996-2024 walk-forward it changes nothing: crustal all-forecast +0.003 (CI [-0.003,+0.009], P 0.83), every M6+ stratum slightly negative but not significant (n=28-49, P 0.06-0.11 = noise, not harm). The reference bit-reproduces the established full-set baseline (0.753, 1151 positives), and the null is robust to the training set -- training on all depths and evaluating on the crustal subset gives +0.001. A univariate diagnostic explains it precisely: the migration geometry IS directionally correct (escalating crustal sequences contract more -- radial-trend mean -0.138 versus -0.094) but weak (single-feature AUC 0.52-0.55), while the foreshock COUNT is strong (AUC 0.694) and already held by the baseline; the geometry therefore adds zero incremental skill. Crustal restriction alone also does not help (0.734 < 0.753). This is real-but-redundant: the only lever in the whole arc with an established real signal contributes nothing beyond what the count features already carry -- a sixth independent saturation line (learned encoder, cross-region, global-scale, source geometry, catalogue density, and now migration geometry) of the location-plus-catalogue paradigm under this target. Recorded as a lever tried and found redundant, not a ceiling; the one residual left open is a SoCal-QTM crustal augmentation of the migration model (a redundancy-driven null makes rescue unlikely but conditional/non-linear value with more positives is not formally excluded), and the search continues for information the catalogue genuinely lacks or a structurally different target.

**2026-07-13 update 20 (target redefinition: a literature reverse-engineering of alternative forecast targets, and the aleatory-ceiling diagnosis that motivates a ground-motion exceedance target).** Six independent saturation lines (rounds 19-24) established that the location-plus-catalogue paradigm is signal-saturated under the current sequence-escalation target, so the next structural lever is the target definition itself. An adversarially-verified literature reverse-engineering (multi-source, 22 confirmed claims) mapped the alternative-target space and closed two candidates. Spatial aftershock-nucleation forecasting, whose published state of the art (DeVries et al. 2018, AUC 0.85) is reproduced exactly by a two-parameter logistic regression on distance and slip (Mignan and Broccardo 2019), is a distance-driven easy-negative artifact that a hard-negative-controlled version would score below, not above. The absolute-magnitude / strong-subsequent target (NESTORE-family) is structurally identical to this project's current escalation label and is statistically power-starved in Japan (single-digit positive clusters), its headline 0.94 accuracy being a class-imbalance majority baseline rather than an AUC. The literature's own top recommendation, the Gulia and Wiemer (2019) b-value foreshock-traffic-light, is already implemented in this pipeline (features_ftls.py, the published early-versus-background b comparison) and contributes +0.001 to the forecast-only AUC, i.e. already null, corroborated by this project's own split-half demonstration that the apparent b-drop is an incompleteness artifact. The decisive diagnosis is that the current target's ~0.75 ceiling is aleatory-dominated rather than epistemic (Lombardi 2017: ETAS parametric uncertainty is far smaller than the process's aleatory variability, so whether a given sequence escalates is a near-memoryless draw once the rate is known), which is exactly why the theoretically-optimal ETAS forward-forecast feature saturates there. The structural response is to redefine the target onto a quantity whose signal is deterministic-physics-dominated rather than aleatory-tail-dominated: a prospective binary forecast of short-term instrumental-intensity exceedance at strong-motion stations within an active sequence, with the threshold placed in the BODY of the intensity distribution (cohort base rate ~20%) so the label is driven by the ETAS-predictable moderate-event rate rather than a single rare-event tail, and with a deterministic magnitude-to-intensity (GMPE + Vs30 site) layer adding an observable, spatially-deterministic prediction axis absent from the purely-temporal escalation label. Hard-negatives are non-exceeding neighbour stations matched on static distance and site so the model cannot solve it by geometry alone, and genuine skill is measured as delta-AUC over a static GMPE/climatology baseline with time- and space-permutation controls -- the pilot gate that must pass before commitment, since the raw AUC will trivially reach 0.90 on the deterministic physics and only the time-varying sequence-state increment counts. Feasibility confirmed: the JMA seismic-intensity database exposes an open, registration-free JSON API (per-station observed intensity for all felt earthquakes), station-window positives on the order of 10^3-10^4 dissolve the small-sample constraint, and the honest-evaluation and walk-forward machinery carries over unchanged. Recorded as the target-redefinition step of the arc -- a planned pivot with its first-gate experiment defined, not a result -- consistent with the standing rule that a high AUC explained by trivial geometry is hollow and only genuine time-varying skill counts.

**2026-07-14 update 21 (ground-motion exceedance -- the pivot's first gate: the genuine time-varying increment is null, so the ground-motion target is a tried-and-missed lever, not a route to 0.90).** The redefined target from update 20 was taken to its gate. Per-station JMA instrumental-intensity exceedance was assembled from the open intensity API for 178 Mm>=6.0 sequences (162,125 station-intensity records, epoch 2011): each station felt in the first 6 h of a sequence is asked whether its shaking in the (6 h, 7 d] forecast window exceeds a threshold, and genuine skill is the increment of the evolving 6 h aftershock-field features over a static geometry baseline (distance-to-mainshock, magnitude, depth, position) in honest temporal walk-forward. On the raw exceedance label the absolute AUC trivially reaches 0.93-0.96 but it is entirely static geometry -- the dynamic increment is -0.006, null -- exactly the hollow-AUC failure mode the standing rule warns about. To make the label itself geometry-free the target was residualised four ways (a mainshock-GMPE residual; a train-fit and a cross-fit HistGBT de-trend of the expected intensity; and a productive-subset restriction), across exceedance thresholds delta 0/0.5/1.0. The genuine dynamic-over-static increment is null in every one. Powered up with an expanding-window blocked-temporal design pooling 88 test sequences and 24,034 station-windows, the increment at the balanced threshold is -0.0004 (CI [-0.065,+0.065]) with static and dynamic models both at AUC ~0.48 on the geometry-free label; an earlier +0.088 on a single 34-sequence split was confirmed to be low-power noise. The adversarial reviewer's steelman -- that genuine skill hides in swarm-like, aftershock-productive sequences where no single dominant source fixes the geometry and is diluted in the pool -- was tested by retraining the whole gate on the high-productivity subset alone, and it too is null (increment -0.023, CI [-0.093,+0.034]). The genuine-label AUC across the family is ~0.48-0.69, an order of magnitude short of 0.90, and no formulation lifts the time-varying increment above zero. Recorded as a lever tried and found null: the ground-motion exceedance target's high absolute AUC is deterministic near-field geometry (the same reject-mode as the 0.5-degree spatial hollow AUC and DeVries 2018), it carries no genuine time-varying forecast increment, and the search continues for a structurally different target -- the remaining unbenchmarked candidates (escalation timing, Bath-law deviation) tested next on the existing catalogue rather than dismissed as aleatory. Not a ceiling claim.

**2026-07-14 update 22 (the two remaining target-redefinition candidates -- escalation timing and Bath-law deviation -- both resolve to null, the Bath apparent-positive caught as a cross-sequence overlap artifact by verifying the reviewer's own clearance rather than trusting it).** With ground-motion closed (update 21), the deep-research map left two unbenchmarked alternative targets, tested here on the existing catalogue rather than dismissed as aleatory. Escalation TIMING -- among sequences that do escalate, whether the strong follow-up onset is imminent (<= tau days) or delayed, from the leak-safe 6 h aftershock field -- is null at every threshold (tau 0.5/1/2 d, pooled blocked-temporal, dynamic-over-static increment +0.02 to +0.045, every CI spanning zero, all AUC ~0.5-0.6): escalation onset is an Omori-memoryless draw that the observed state does not sharpen. Bath-law DEVIATION -- forecasting the size of the eventual largest aftershock (Dm = Mm - largest forecast-window aftershock, Bath ~ 1.2) from the 6 h field -- first looked positive: a +0.077 dynamic-over-static increment (AUC 0.60 to 0.68, N=616) that survived a train-only-median leak-guard, an ablation dropping the early-largest-aftershock feature, and a row-permutation null, and that an adversarial review reproduced and cleared as a genuine ETAS-productivity signal. Verifying that clearance rather than trusting it, a strict-independence filter that drops every sequence whose space-time window contains another sequence's mainshock (212 of 616) collapses the increment to -0.023 (CI [-0.065,+0.018]) on the 404 contamination-free sequences: the entire +0.077 came from overlapping sequences where the 6 h field and the forecast-window largest aftershock share events from a different nearby cluster -- shared-event contamination, not forecast skill, a within-block row-level artifact that both the block-boundary reasoning and the global permutation-null miss, the same failure family as the retracted joint-fusion leaks. Both candidates recorded null. Taken with the six catalogue-saturation lines and the ground-motion residual, the catalogue-derived target-redefinition space is now mapped: every reformulation reduces to the same genuine-but-aleatory-capped ~0.75 ETAS-context/productivity signal or is null. Not a ceiling claim -- it records that redefining the target on the catalogue alone does not open a genuine 0.90 route, and the remaining structural levers are a new observation system that densifies or adds a non-catalogue channel (template-matched microseismicity in the first 6 h; near-fault real-time strain or GNSS) or the untested GPU-scale sequence-transformer regime, which the search turns to next.

**2026-07-14 update 23 (next structural lever after the catalogue target-space is mapped: a self-supervised catalogue foundation model -- launched, pilot in progress, not yet a result).** Updates 18-22 established that every catalogue-derived target reduces to the same genuine-but-aleatory-capped ~0.75 ETAS signal or is null, so the next lever is not another target but a different way of extracting the catalogue: a learned representation that could capture DEPARTURES from ETAS (anisotropic triggering, fault-structure-dependent decay, foreshock-specific patterns) which the parametric point-process model, near-optimal for its own form, cannot. Round 19's small supervised two-stream GRU (AUC 0.722, below the 0.753 hand-feature stack) already probed this and under-performed, but its ceiling was the tiny labelled set (1097 sequences); the untested regime is self-supervised PRETRAINING on the full catalogue, where labels are not the bottleneck. The corpus is 2.45M JMA events (867k at M>=2) tokenised into 36,115 fixed-length event-sequence windows, over which a small transformer encoder is pretrained by masked-event reconstruction (no escalation labels), then frozen and used to embed each sequence's first-6h stream; the pilot gate is whether that embedding, added to the confirmed ETAS-context stack, lifts the pooled all-forecast AUC above the established ~0.753 in honest walk-forward. Recorded honestly as a launched experiment with its gate defined, not a result -- and with the standing caveat that if the catalogue's information is genuinely aleatory-capped, even a foundation model returns ~0.75, which would itself be an informative closure pointing the search decisively to non-catalogue observation channels. The pilot runs on CPU as a lower bound on representation learning; a positive signal would justify scaling on GPU, a null a decisive record that catalogue representation does not open the 0.90 route. Not a ceiling claim -- an experiment in flight.

**2026-07-15 update 24 (the catalogue foundation model, frozen-embedding pilot: null -- the pretrained representation is redundant with the ETAS stack, a lower-bound closure that points to non-catalogue channels).** The step-3 gate from update 23 was run. Each escalation sequence's first-6h in-disc event stream was rebuilt in the encoder's own 5-feature window-relative format, standardised with the pretraining-corpus statistics, padded to length 64, passed through the frozen masked-event-pretrained encoder (best validation reconstruction 0.7137), and mean-pooled to a 96-dimensional embedding; a HistGBT was then fit on the confirmed ETAS-context stack with versus without the embedding in paired eleven-fold walk-forward (the two folds whose build directories had been reclaimed by disk cleanup were dropped, leaving a paired identical-fold comparison so the delta is unbiased, and the no-embedding arm reproduced the saved fold scores bit-for-bit on all eleven folds, confirming the reproduction). The increment is null: the raw 96-dimensional embedding gives -0.0063 (a tree-split dilution of the 40-feature stack, since the compact train-fit PCA-8 form lands at -0.0008 with a confidence interval spanning zero, an exact null), the embedding alone scores AUC 0.544 (barely above chance and fully redundant with the ETAS features once combined), and the M6+ layers are null. This is the seventh convergent saturation and mirrors round 19 exactly: both a from-scratch supervised sequence model and a frozen self-supervised representation converge to redundant-with-ETAS, so the catalogue event sequence -- however it is encoded -- carries no short-term escalation signal beyond ETAS in this Japanese data. Recorded as a tried-and-missed lever, not a ceiling: the pilot closes the cheap frozen-embedding bet and is a lower bound on representation learning (a full unfrozen end-to-end fine-tune at larger GPU scale is a distinct untested regime that the seven convergent nulls weigh against but do not disprove), and the informative closure is that catalogue representation does not open the 0.90 route, pointing the search to non-catalogue observation channels. Not a ceiling claim.

**2026-07-15 update 25 (the foundation model's unfrozen end-to-end fine-tune, at the current scale and at a larger model+corpus scale, is also null -- the catalogue-representation-scaling direction is closed).** The frozen-embedding null (update 24) left two objections: a frozen encoder cannot adapt to the task, and only the small RPi5-pretrained encoder was tested. Both were closed on free-tier Kaggle GPU (no paid compute). The pretrained encoder was unfrozen and trained end-to-end on the escalation label -- its first-6h stream embedding concatenated with the confirmed ETAS stack through an MLP head, per fold on year<split with a leak-free temporal early-stop -- in two arms: the small d96/3L encoder, and a larger d192/6L/8H encoder pretrained on GPU on a four-times-larger corpus (188,890 windows from 1.51M M>=1.5 events, whose validation reconstruction of 0.68 versus the small encoder's 0.71 confirms it genuinely learned a better representation). Both are null: the fine-tuned network alone scores 0.73 (small) and 0.73 (big), below the confirmed GBT stack's 0.753, and the 50/50 rank-blend merely recovers the baseline (small +0.0036, CI [-0.0023, +0.0094], P 0.887; big +0.0002, CI [-0.0064, +0.0067], P 0.510). The M6+ layer point estimates are small-positive but non-significant (n=32, confidence intervals spanning zero, P around 0.82-0.87), consistent with the recurring small-sample-noise pattern and recorded as not a finding. So unfreezing does not help and neither does scaling the model and the pretraining corpus -- the better reconstruction of the bigger encoder does not translate into any escalation skill. Taken with the frozen pilot and round 19's from-scratch sequence model, the catalogue sequence representation adds nothing genuine over the ETAS stack whether frozen, fine-tuned, or scaled up, so the "scale would help" hypothesis is now tested and null and the foundation-model / catalogue-representation-scaling direction is closed. Not a ceiling claim -- a tried-and-missed lever; the genuine remaining information is a non-catalogue observation channel, which the search turns to next.

**2026-07-15 update 26 (non-catalogue observation channels: the two physical candidates exist but have neither an openly downloadable dense feed nor any published forecast skill, so the openly-executable lever set is for now mapped -- not a ceiling).** With the catalogue-representation direction closed (updates 18-25), the remaining genuine information is a non-catalogue observation channel. A multi-source, adversarially-verified review of the openly-accessible options for Japan examined the two physically-motivated candidates: continuous near-fault crustal strain and tilt (NIED Hi-net borehole tiltmeters, JMA Tokai volumetric strainmeters) and continuous groundwater level (the AIST/Geological Survey of Japan observation-well network). Both exist as coordinated instrument networks, but neither has any published demonstration of short-term forecast skill above an ETAS baseline under hard-negative control; the demonstrated state is uniformly retrospective, detection-capability, or hypothetical-preslip simulation, and the single strongest result is a hard null (NIED Hi-net borehole tiltmeters recorded no clear precursory tilt or preslip before the 2011 Mw9.0 Tohoku earthquake, corroborated by a 2024 re-analysis that also dissolves a competing GNSS preslip claim). A direct feasibility check then found no openly downloadable dense feed for either channel: the dense nationwide Hi-net tiltmeter channel is not exposed for programmatic download (only the seismic waveforms are), and the openly-licensed AIST/GSJ strain, tilt, and groundwater data is served through a plotting viewer with request-gated raw time series and is regionally sparse. So the two candidate channels are neither pre-validated as forecasters nor openly-and-densely accessible, and the openly-executable lever set is, for now, mapped. This is recorded as the current state of the open-data search, not a ceiling claim: the goal -- a genuine hard-negative-controlled short-term escalation AUC of 0.90 -- remains open and awaits a genuinely new openly-executable channel or method, while the operational 7-day and monthly ETAS forecasts continue to run.

**2026-07-15 update 27 (a new well-powered lever: surface-deformation escalation forecasting from open InSAR via COMET LiCSAR -- launched; feature extraction and the skill test are next).** With the catalogue-representation direction closed, the remaining genuine information is the surface deformation the catalogue discards, and the openly-accessible dense source for it over Japan is COMET LiCSAR: analysis-ready Sentinel-1 geocoded interferograms, coherence, and look-vector layers, downloadable without any gating from the open product tree (the NASA OPERA surface-displacement product does not yet cover Japan, so LiCSAR is used). A Japan frame index was built by crawling the product tree and filtering frame footprints to the Japan bounding box, yielding 66 frames across 22 Sentinel-1 relative-orbit tracks. Crucially, and unlike the earlier point-geodesy channels (offshore seafloor GNSS-A with 17 events, borehole pore pressure with 2), the escalation test on this channel is well-powered: of the independent M>=4.5 mainshocks in the Sentinel-1 era (2016 onward) that fall inside a Japan frame, 889 have surface-deformation coverage with 233 escalation-positive, and the crustal subset (depth <=30 km, where surface InSAR is most relevant) has 393 with 130 positive. The plan is to extract, for each sequence, the pre-mainshock line-of-sight surface deformation in the epicentral area -- velocity, recent acceleration, and the spatial gradient of displacement as a strain-rate proxy, with coherence and atmospheric masking and the look-vector conversion from line-of-sight to displacement components -- add it to the confirmed ETAS stack, and test in leak-free, hard-negative-controlled walk-forward whether it lifts the pooled all-forecast AUC above the established 0.753. No prior work has tested InSAR surface deformation as a short-term sequence-escalation forecaster on a hard-negative-controlled sample of this size. Recorded as a launched, well-powered experiment, with feature extraction and the skill test as the immediate next steps.

**2026-07-16 update 28 (InSAR lever, step 1: the true-footprint sample is 491 sequences / 108 escalation-positive — smaller than the update-27 bounding-box estimate but still well-powered; leak-safe feature extraction is running).** The update-27 power figures (889 sequences / 233 positive; crustal 393/130) were computed against frame *bounding boxes*. Testing each epicenter against the true frame footprint polygons (`metadata/<frame>-poly.txt`, point-in-polygon over all 66 Japan frames) reduces the covered sample to **491 sequences with 108 escalation-positive** (crustal depth ≤30 km: 145 with 40 positive): Sentinel-1 swaths are diagonal, so bounding boxes overcount, and offshore epicenters outside the imaged area drop out. This is still an order of magnitude more positives than any point-geodesy channel tested here (seafloor GNSS-A: 17 events; borehole pore pressure: 2). Extraction of the pre-mainshock signal is running: for each covered sequence, interferograms whose *both* acquisitions predate the mainshock by at least one day (strictly pre-event, hence known at forecast time — no leak), within a 150-day lookback and up to a 48-day temporal baseline, are pulled from the CEDA archive tree, and the epicentral line-of-sight displacement is measured as the median over a ±0.10° box referenced against a 0.15–0.35° ring (differencing out long-wavelength atmosphere; GACOS correction is a planned refinement), with the unwrapped-phase nodata mask applied and a least-squares plane fit supplying a spatial-gradient (strain-rate proxy) feature. The walk-forward harness (8 InSAR columns appended to the confirmed stack, joined by a fold-invariant physical event key) is staged and verified: the new fold script's reference model bit-reproduces the round-22 reference (max abs score diff 0.0), and the pre-registered primary endpoint is the pooled all-forecast delta within the covered cohort. One methodological note worth recording: the internal `ms_idx` event key is *not* invariant across fold directories built on different catalogue epochs (zero agreement between a cat-1990 and a cat-2000 fold), so the InSAR join uses the physical (time, latitude, longitude, magnitude) key instead; a re-check of the round-22 focal join, which used `ms_idx`, confirmed its lookup table contained both keyspaces and agreed on 6181/6213 common events, so the round-22 null stands.

**2026-07-17 update 29 (InSAR lever, result: the pre-registered covered-cohort test is null at current coverage — and the honest reading is *underpowered*, not closed; the extraction and harness are sound and the lever stays open at better coverage).** The extraction completed cleanly: 11,046 strictly pre-mainshock interferogram measurements over 345 of the 491 covered sequences (the rest fail the pixel-count quality thresholds or have no qualifying pair in the 150-day window). On the pre-registered primary endpoint — the pooled all-forecast AUC delta within the InSAR-covered cohort, both positives and negatives restricted to covered events — the eight-feature model changes nothing: delta −0.004 with a 95% bootstrap interval of [−0.027, +0.020] against the covered-cohort base of 0.746 (52 positives, 265 negatives). A signed-feature variant (retaining the line-of-sight sign of the primary-frame velocity and acceleration, which the absolute-value aggregation had discarded — an adversarial-review finding) is equally null (−0.005 [−0.028, +0.020]), and the crustal subset's positive point estimate (+0.02–0.04) sits inside a wide interval on 16 positives. The decisive caveat, raised by adversarial review and confirmed by direct recomputation, is *power*: only the 2018 and 2020 folds ever train a live InSAR model, and their training sets contain just 1.8% and 3.6% covered events, because Sentinel-1 coverage starts in 2016 and walk-forward training must precede the test window; the 2016 fold (21 of the 52 covered positives) has zero covered training events, so its variant is the reference by construction and mechanically freezes a quarter of the cohort at delta zero, halving the apparent interval width. Recomputed on the two live folds only, the honest headline is −0.002 [−0.035, +0.035] on 31 positives — an interval that cannot exclude effects of ±0.03 in either direction. Verification: no leak (both acquisitions strictly pre-event, median data-end five days before the mainshock), no masking bug (the augmented model genuinely moves essentially every covered score; the physical-key join is collision-free at 345/345), and every headline number was re-run twice bit-identically. Recorded as a lever *tried at current open-data coverage*: the binding constraint is that LiCSAR frames cover 491 of ~6,500 stack events, and the named next steps that would thicken the covered cohort are on-demand open Sentinel-1 processing (ASF HyP3) or the ARIA-S1-GUNW standard product for events outside LiCSAR frames, GACOS tropospheric correction plus coherence masking to cut per-pair noise, and a 2022/2024 re-split of the last fold so that later test years see the accumulated covered training data.

Two methodological artifacts were responsible for all false positives found during the investigation:

1. **Aftershock contamination**: Without isolating independent events, clustering inflates apparent signals (b-value: 90% → 15%, Kp -12h: 62% → 11%)
2. **Sampling bias**: Using chronologically-first events over-samples the 2011 Tohoku aftershock cluster (TEC σ: 0.942 → 0.263)

### Phase 1: Single indicators — all negative

**b-value (Gutenberg-Richter) — ❌ Aftershock artifact**

| Window | Random b<0.7 | All M5+ b<0.7 | Isolated M5+ b<0.7 |
|---|---|---|---|
| 7-day | 16.9% | 90.0% | **15.2%** (= random) |
| 30-day | 42.6% | 91.6% | **39.5%** (= random) |
| 90-day | 72.2% | 84.6% | **55.1%** (noise range) |

**Epicenter TEC (raw) — ❌ Systematic bias**

Random TEC drops *more* than pre-earthquake TEC (σ=-0.781 vs -0.222). Bias from seasonal/diurnal/solar cycle patterns.

**Multi-indicator grid search (100 combos) — ❌ No signal**

Best lift 1.82 at n=17. Fixed thresholds: earthquake 22.1% vs random 21.4% — identical.

### Phase 2: Candidate signals found → validated → all rejected

Two promising signals were identified during exploratory analysis. Both were then rigorously validated with aftershock isolation + balanced time sampling + alternative methods + bootstrap CI. **Both collapsed.**

**Kp -12h geomagnetic spike — ❌ Aftershock chain artifact (confirmed)**

| Lead time | All events Kp>3 | **Isolated events Kp>3** | Random Kp>3 |
|---|---|---|---|
| -24h | 55.9% | **12.2%** | 14.2% |
| -12h | 61.5% | **10.8%** | 14.0% |
| -6h | 55.1% | **10.0%** | 15.2% |

The apparent 62% Kp>3 rate was entirely from aftershock chains: the first M5+ in a cluster occurs during a Kp storm, then subsequent events in the same cluster all inherit the high Kp. Isolated events show Kp *below* random at every lead time.

**TEC detrended (seasonal correction) — ❌ Sampling bias + aftershock artifact (confirmed)**

| Condition | Before bias fix | **After bias fix** | Bootstrap p |
|---|---|---|---|
| Random | σ=+0.247, spikes 15.6% | σ=+0.247, spikes 15.6% | — |
| All M5+ | **σ=+0.942, spikes 56.5%** | σ=+0.279, spikes 19.5% | p=0.265 |
| **Isolated M5+ only** | not tested | **σ=+0.263, spikes 15.0%** | **p=0.389** |

The σ=0.942 "discovery" had two compounding artifacts:
- `target_events[:500]` selected chronologically-first events, biased toward 2011 Tohoku aftershock cluster
- Non-isolated events carried residual clustering effects

After balanced time sampling + isolation filter: mean_diff=0.016, 95% CI=[-0.106, +0.137], **indistinguishable from random**.

**Validation: temporal stability — ❌ No signal in either period**

| Period | Isolated TECσ | Random TECσ | Bootstrap p |
|---|---|---|---|
| 2011-2018 (n=1937) | 0.218 | 0.312 | p=0.833 |
| 2019-2026 (n=1178) | 0.095 | 0.183 | p=0.841 |

Isolated events show *lower* TEC than random in both periods.

**Validation: alternative detrending (30-day rolling) — ❌ Zero spikes**

| Condition | Rolling σ | Spikes (σ>+1) |
|---|---|---|
| Random | -0.666 | 0.0% |
| Isolated M5+ | -0.622 | 0.0% |

Independent detrending method confirms no signal.

**Validation: magnitude dependence (with isolation) — ❌ No monotonic increase**

| Magnitude | Isolated TECσ | Spikes |
|---|---|---|
| M5-5.9 (n=1373 iso) | 0.127 | 11.7% |
| M6-6.9 (n=160 iso) | 0.083 | 10.1% |
| M7+ (n=20 iso) | 0.370 | 20.0% |

M6 is *weaker* than M5. No physically consistent magnitude scaling.

### Key lessons

1. **Aftershock isolation is essential** — without it, every indicator shows inflated signals due to temporal clustering
2. **Sampling method matters** — chronological truncation (`[:N]`) can introduce severe bias when event rates are non-stationary (e.g., post-Tohoku)
3. **Low-resolution global indices cannot detect local precursors** — IONEX TEC (2.5°×5° grid) and Kp (global 3-hour average) spatially average away any local earthquake-related signal
4. **Always validate with multiple independent methods** — the TEC signal survived aftershock filtering OR sampling correction alone, but collapsed under both simultaneously

### Phase 2: Physics-based and statistical approaches — 3 signals found

Phase 1's fundamental limitation was **spatial resolution** — global indices dilute local signals below detection. Phase 2 attacks from 4 independent directions. Three produced signals:

**Coulomb stress transfer — CFS threshold-dependent lift (spatial control applied)**

Using Okada (1992) dislocation model with 3,060 GCMT focal mechanisms. Compared earthquake locations vs 2-5° shifted locations (controls for spatial clustering):

| CFS threshold | Earthquake % | Shifted 2-5° % | Lift |
|---|---|---|---|
| > 10 kPa | 63.7% | 68.6% | 0.93 (no signal) |
| > 100 kPa | 45.4% | 22.9% | **1.98** |
| > 500 kPa | 23.4% | 5.3% | **4.43** |
| > 1000 kPa | 14.7% | 2.4% | **6.03** |

Low CFS thresholds show no signal (spatial clustering effect). **High CFS (>500 kPa) shows 4-6x lift even after spatial control** — earthquakes preferentially occur at *exact* stress-enhanced locations, not just the same general region.

**Seismicity rate anomaly — 6.7x activation lift (model-free)**

Regional M3+ rate in 7 days before each M5+ event vs long-term regional average:

| Condition | Activation (>2x rate) | Quiescence (<0.5x rate) |
|---|---|---|
| Before M5+ | **47.0%** | 23.0% |
| Random | 7.0% | 75.4% |
| **Lift** | **6.71** | 0.31 |

47% of M5+ events are preceded by at least 2x normal seismicity rate in their region.

**Spatiotemporal clustering — lift 2.83, p=0.0 (validated)**

Zaliapin & Ben-Zion (2013) nearest-neighbor distance clustering:

| | Has foreshock sequence | Mean foreshock count |
|---|---|---|
| M5+ events | **14.7%** | 9.19 |
| Random M4 | 5.2% | 2.17 |
| **Lift** | **2.83** | — |

Bootstrap 95% CI: [2.01, 4.49], p=0.0. Temporally stable: 2011-2018 = 16.1%, 2019-2026 = 12.3%. Magnitude-dependent: M5 = 14.1% → M6 = 21.2%.

**High-resolution GNSS-TEC — data unavailable**

Nagoya University ISEE archive URLs returned 404 for all attempted date patterns. URL investigation needed.

### Phase 2.5: Aftershock bias validation — all 3 signals survived

Critical question: are the 3 signals independent, or just aftershock cascading? **All survived the same isolation filter that destroyed Phase 1.**

**Isolation test — signals persist for independent (non-aftershock) M5+ events**

| Signal | All M5+ | **Isolated M5+** | Random | **Isolated lift** |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| CFS > 500 kPa | 18.3% | **7.5%** | 0.2% | **37.5** |
| Activation > 2x | 47.0% | **14.9%** | 8.0% | **1.86** |
| Has foreshock | 68.3% | **42.8%** | 10.4% | **4.12** |

Phase 1's TEC detrended signal (σ=0.942) collapsed to σ=0.263 (p=0.389) under isolation. Phase 2's signals maintained significant lifts (37.5x, 1.86x, 4.12x).

**Time delay — isolated events show long-term Coulomb triggering (median 333 days)**

| Condition | Median delay | < 30 days | > 90 days | > 365 days |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| All M5+ | 161 days | 32.8% | 57.8% | 34.2% |
| **Isolated M5+** | **333 days** | **10.0%** | **77.5%** | **47.2%** |
| CFS > 500 kPa | 6 days | 62.4% | 32.2% | 19.9% |

Isolated events occur a median of 333 days after their nearest prior M5+ — not aftershocks but **delayed stress-triggered events**. 77.5% occur more than 90 days later.

**Signal correlation — partially independent (ratio 2.12)**

| Metric | Value |
|---|---|
| P(all 3) if independent | 12.2% |
| P(all 3) observed | 25.9% |
| Correlation ratio | **2.12** |

Ratio of 2.12 means signals are **moderately correlated but not redundant**. They contain partially independent information — combining them is meaningful.

**Prospective test — combined score lift 20.66 in unseen data**

Combined score: count of (CFS>100, rate>2x, has foreshock) per event.

| Score | Train 2011-2018 | **Test 2019-2026** | Random |
|---|---|---|---|
| 0 (no signals) | 22.9% | 31.7% | **84.0%** |
| 1 | 15.6% | 27.2% | 13.4% |
| 2 | 24.0% | **33.9%** | 2.4% |
| 3 (all signals) | 37.5% | 7.2% | 0.2% |

Test period: 41.1% of M5+ events have score ≥ 2, vs 2.6% of random locations → **lift 20.66**. The model generalizes to unseen time periods.

### Phase 3a: Catalog-based methods — mostly negative

Three additional methods using existing earthquake catalog only (no new data). None added significant prediction power beyond Phase 2.

**LURR (Load-Unload Response Ratio) — ❌ No signal**

| Window | EQ LURR>1.5 | Random | Lift |
|---|---|---|---|
| 30 days | 26.3% | 55.0% | 0.48 |
| 90 days | 31.6% | 36.9% | 0.86 |
| 180 days | 28.3% | 30.2% | 0.94 |

Tidal stress asymmetry shows no earthquake-specific pattern. Random locations have equal or higher LURR values.

**Natural Time Analysis — ❌ No signal**

κ1 variance near critical value (0.070) is equally common before M5+ events and at random times (lift 0.84-1.19 across all window sizes).

**Earthquake Nowcasting — ⚠️ Weak signal (lift 1.31)**

EPS > 70 before M5+ events: 26.8% vs 20.4% random (lift 1.31). Weak magnitude dependence (M7+: 35.7%). Insufficient for standalone prediction but may complement Phase 2 signals.

### Phase 3b: Independent physical observations (in progress)

The critical next step: **non-seismological data** that is physically independent from Phase 2's earthquake-catalog-based signals.

| Parameter | Physical mechanism | Data source | Status |
|---|---|---|---|
| **MODIS thermal IR** | Stress → gas release → surface heating (LAIC model) | ORNL DAAC TESViS API (no auth, 1km) | **359 records fetched**, analysis script ready |
| **ULF magnetic field** | Stress → piezoelectric/electrokinetic emission | INTERMAGNET BGS GIN + WDC Kyoto | Fetcher rewritten, testing |
| **S-net ocean bottom pressure** | Slow-slip → seafloor displacement | NIED Hi-net portal (150 stations) | Registration needed |
| GEONET GPS-TEC (per-station) | Point TEC above epicenters | GSI GEONET RINEX | Nagoya Univ. 404, alternative needed |
| Radon / He isotopes | Fault degassing | AIST monitoring | Limited access |

**MODIS LST analysis** (Tronin 2006, Ouzounov & Freund 2004): For each M5.5+ earthquake on land, MODIS Land Surface Temperature is extracted at the epicenter ±14 days. Anomaly detection uses standardized deviation from local baseline (RST/RETIRA method, Tramutoli 2005). Tests pre-event anomaly, isolation filter, magnitude/depth dependence, and temporal profile.

**ULF magnetic analysis** (Hayakawa et al. 2007, Hattori 2004): Analyzes 1-minute geomagnetic data from KAK/MMB/KNY for three precursor signatures: (1) ULF Z-component spectral power increase, (2) Sz/Sh polarization ratio > 1 (lithospheric origin), (3) fractal dimension decrease. Nighttime-only (0-6 LT) to avoid anthropogenic noise.

### Phase 3b: Independent physical observations — MODIS ❌, ULF ⚠️

**MODIS Land Surface Temperature — ❌ No thermal precursor signal**

Pre-earthquake 7-day anomaly: mean=0.061σ, 95% CI=[-0.109, 0.224], >2σ = 0.0%. The LAIC thermal precursor hypothesis (Tronin 2006) is not supported in this dataset.

**ULF Magnetic — ⚠️ Strong retrospective signal, forward evaluation pending**

| Station | Events | Power ratio (pre/post) | Sz/Sh polarization | Fractal dim |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| KAK | 439 | **mean 7.9x**, >2x = 53% | pre=0.98 > post=0.34 | pre=1.27 < post=1.33 |

All three ULF precursor signatures are present (power increase, lithospheric polarization, fractal regularization). **However, data covers only 2011-01-05 to 2011-05-05 (80 days including Tohoku M9)** — aftershock contamination is almost certain. Full-period data needed for prospective evaluation.

### Phase 4: Prospective (forward-looking) prediction — **gain up to 7.8x**

The fundamental shift: from "given earthquake, was there anomaly?" to **"given anomaly now, will earthquake follow?"** Evaluated on 2019-2026 (unseen data), with spatially-resolved base rates per 2°×2° cell.

| Signal | Alarms | Precision | Recall | **Prob. Gain** | IGPE (bits) |
|---|---|---|---|---|---|
| **Combined (ETAS+CFS+fore) ≥2** | **16** | **62.5%** | 2.5% | **7.8x** | **2.96** |
| ETAS residual > 5x | 38 | 52.6% | 6.8% | 4.0x | 1.99 |
| Foreshock ≥ 10 | 74 | 39.2% | 8.8% | **5.1x** | 2.36 |
| Foreshock ≥ 5 | 257 | 34.2% | 16.3% | 4.1x | 2.04 |
| ETAS residual > 3x | 71 | 47.9% | 8.2% | 3.8x | 1.92 |
| Rate > 5x | 464 | 19.0% | 14.4% | 4.2x | 2.09 |
| Cumulative CFS > 100 kPa | 440 | 19.8% | 3.7% | 2.4x | 1.25 |

**Key finding**: When ETAS residual, cumulative CFS, and foreshock alarms fire simultaneously, 62.5% of the time an M5+ earthquake follows within 7 days — **7.8 times better than random**. The ETAS residual (rate exceeding aftershock model prediction) is the strongest individual signal at 52.6% precision.

**Pattern Informatics (Rundle 2003)**: Prospective Molchan AUC = 0.349 (< 0.5 = better than random). PI hotspots preferentially attract future M5+ events. Top hotspots: Iburi (42.75°N), Izu-Bonin (32.75°N, 29.75°N).

### 2026-06: Skill decomposition — what the AUC actually measures

A systematic audit (2026-06-08) of where the monthly-forecast skill comes from, using an independently harvested complete ISC/JMA M3+ catalogue (108,808 events) and region-split walk-forward evaluation:

- **Offshore AUC 0.83 > onshore 0.72** (M5+/34d, cells split by GNSS-station presence as a crustal/subduction proxy). The pooled 0.79-0.87 is dominated by "the next M5+ in already-active subduction zones" — aftershock clustering, not rare-mainshock precursors.
- **19 current-activity features (rate / ETAS residual / days-since / neighbour rate) match the full 85-feature set.** The other 66 — b-value, CFS, Pattern Informatics, Benioff strain, and *every* exogenous channel (cosmic ray, geomagnetic ULF, OLR, SO2, soil moisture, cloud, X-ray, ionospheric TEC, S-net VLF, lightning, GNSS strain) — contribute net zero or negative. Onshore, the 44 exogenous features alone score **AUC 0.517 ≈ coin flip**.
- **A single clustering feature (pi_score, AUC 0.770) nearly matches the full 85-feature GBT (0.79)**; features + ML add only ~+0.02 on top of it.
- **A static spatial climatology (per-cell 2011-2020 M5+ frequency, time-invariant) scores AUC 0.862** on the 2020-2026 test labels — 0.009 below the 0.871 GBT ceiling. Pooled AUC is saturated by the "Tohoku-oki is always active" map.
- The temporal skill that remains is **sparse but real**: given an M5+ in a cell, the next-7-day M5+ probability is **2.2x** baseline (Omori clustering). It is concentrated in post-mainshock windows (~2% of cell-time), which is why it barely moves a pooled all-window AUC.

**Complete-catalogue precursor precision (buildup watch)**: rate-ratio buildup precursors are real but specific to shallow crustal earthquakes — Noto 2024 M7.5 ranks **1st of 114 cells with 32x lift using only data up to 30 days before**, and Kumamoto 2016 shows a 483x fused anomaly; subduction M7s show no catalogue precursor (activity saturation at 400-934 events/yr). Operating point: recall ~18%, lift ~2.6-3x, false-alarm rate ~7%.

**GNSS strain channel (NGL tenv3, 1,217 Japanese stations) — publication-grade null** (2026-06-08): strain-anomaly fusion correctly ranks Noto 2024 M7.5 #1 one month ahead and diagnoses the documented slow-slip precursor, but in systematic prospective evaluation it never beats seismicity-only scoring across months, and adding real GEONET-derived features to the ML changes AUC by −0.0007. Physically real, case-diagnostic, zero aggregate forecast skill.

### 2026-06: CSEP information gain — the right metric, and where ETAS wins

Pooled AUC saturates on spatial climatology and under-measures temporal skill. Re-evaluating on the CSEP standard axis — Poisson forecast log-likelihood gain over the time-invariant climatology baseline — fit on 2012-2020, scored prospectively on 2020-2026 (M3.5+ driver catalogue, 54,075 events; M5+ targets):

| Model | Information gain (nats/event) | Probability gain |
|---|---|---|
| Gridded ETAS (2°/daily, proper likelihood fit) | +0.46 | 1.58x |
| **Continuous grid-free ETAS (point-process MLE)** | **+3.63** | median 2.52x |
| **+ regional kernels (crustal vs subduction)** | **+3.69** | median 3.11x |
| Post-mainshock regime (<7d, <100 km of M≥6) | +9.10 | ~9000x (n=92) |

- The continuous model recovers textbook physics (Omori p=1.15, no degenerate parameters) and 100% of test events score above climatology. Continuous (per-event) and gridded (cell-window) evaluation frames differ, so the rows are not strictly comparable — the robust statement is that both beat climatology prospectively and gridding destroys most of the resolvable skill.
- **The regional split is real physics**: subduction kernels fit larger aftershock zones, stronger magnitude scaling and faster Omori decay than crustal ones (+0.055 nats, train and test agree; offshore-target IG 4.01 > onshore 3.48).
- Anisotropic (trench-elongated) kernels and spatially-varying b-value magnitude forecasting were both tested and rejected (overfit −0.009 / aggregate null +0.0005, with one weak real signal: causal b drops to 0.86 before M≥6.5 vs 0.94 before M5-6).
- Short-horizon research validation: weekly 7-day M5+ maps at 0.5° resolution score **1.83x climatology overall and 6.9x in post-mainshock windows** (0.25°: 1.94x / 15.9x, post-mainshock alerting only). A USGS near-real-time driver variant loses little (1.67x / 6.8x), so the approach survives on a live feed.
- **Operationally integrated (2026-06-17)**: the regional crustal/subduction split is now a live feature in the monthly gridded outlook (`operational_forecast.py`, which commits to `forecasts/`). Two onshore/offshore-driven regional-ETAS rate features — re-fit on the operational USGS M≥4 driver catalogue — were added to the existing 6-kernel + background feature set. A 10-fold walk-forward backtest (baseline reproduces the deployed OOS AUC 0.863) shows a small but consistent gain on the metric that matters: **CSEP information gain +94 nats over the backtest (+0.013/hit), OOS AUC 0.863→0.865**. AUC barely moves because it saturates on spatial climatology; the regional split's contribution is in dynamic/temporal skill, which the information-gain axis captures. Modest in absolute terms but real and physically grounded — the uniform heuristic kernels cannot express region-dependent triggering. Graceful fallback to the original kernel set if the fitted-parameter file is absent.

**Conclusion of the arc**: earthquake forecast skill exists and decomposes cleanly — a static hazard map is an AUC-0.86 product; properly-fit ETAS aftershock forecasting adds a genuine 1.6-3x (post-mainshock ~10x) probability gain on top; exogenous precursor channels add nothing measurable in aggregate. The catalogue/ETAS occurrence axis is at its ceiling.

### 2026-06: Next frontier — nucleation from raw waveforms (both episodes complete - five pre-registered nulls, a sixth b-value test [retrospective asperity only], a seventh below-catalogue tremor test [0/3], and an eighth dv/v velocity-change test [0/2], a ninth self-supervised waveform-embedding test [Kumamoto, null], and a tenth multi-case extension [Iquique, null], and an eleventh geodetic GNSS test [Kumamoto 5-min kinematic, null - raw and common-mode-filtered], and a twelfth seafloor-OBP verification [2018 Boso SSE, real OBP + open ocean model, null - reproducible detection floor ~Mw6.5], and a thirteenth multi-case floor-vs-network curve [Cascadia/Guerrero/Hikurangi + Boso onshore & OBP, noise-limited floor Mw~5.3-6.4 but realization set by near-field coverage - Hikurangi's documented Mw7.0 is invisible onshore], and a fourteenth borehole-strainmeter modality [2012 Cascadia ETS, detected 8 sigma via an inverse-variance strain-tensor matched filter, floor ~0.25 Mw below GNSS at matched geometry - overturns the earlier strainmeter dead-end], then the curve hardened by a fifth plate boundary [Nicoya 2007+2009 Costa Rica, onshore-over-slip detected, spatial pattern r=0.87 perm p<0.003], a full spatial-pattern + permutation audit of every detection [Boso/Bungo/Manawatu/Nicoya/Guerrero confirmed, Cascadia GNSS downgraded to spatially-unconfirmed, Hikurangi null confirmed at the pattern level], a sensitivity-at-slip mechanism [offshore slip ~30x below the onshore-detectable level explains the null], and a distributed-slip inversion [Boso data-driven Mw6.5 = catalog, no assumed area], a fifteenth InSAR modality [2018 Boso + Guerrero SSE, open Sentinel-1 troposphere/separation-limited null], a sixteenth offshore near-field test [S-net seafloor, the three largest S-net-era M7+ events (Miyako/Aomori/Fukushima) all NULL, extended below catalogue completeness by matched-filter with an aftershock positive control], and a seventeenth onshore Hi-net dense-array test [2016 Kumamoto M6.5, the deepest open-data injection floor (dM-5.0, ~ML1-2) and a power-calibrated null on foreshock-rate acceleration], and an eighteenth onshore high-density case [2019 Ridgecrest M7.1 (SCSN), the same powered null shown robust to both a stationary and an Omori-decaying baseline (last-3 h p=0.23-0.27), self-injection floor dM-4.5], and a nineteenth b-value FTLS test [2019 Ridgecrest M6.4 to M7.1, the Gulia and Wiemer (2019, Nature) foreshock-traffic-light showcase: no prospective foreshock b-drop with independent magnitudes, incompleteness-robust b-positive stays ~0.9 to the final approach, corroborating the Dascher-Cousineau 2020 parameter-sensitivity critique], and a twentieth b-value FTLS test [2016 Amatrice-Visso-Norcia Mw6.5, the third Gulia and Wiemer (2019, Nature) foreshock-traffic-light showcase and the only one where the B1 relative-drop is computable (real pre-Amatrice background): the Aki foreshock RED light (b 0.72, -27.5% vs background) is an incompleteness artifact (the robust b-positive is a normal 1.14, invariant to completeness), the operational [Visso, Norcia] window is flat-to-rising (1.09 to 1.21), the apparent rate acceleration is the intervening Visso Mw5.9 aftershock sequence (two-term Amatrice+Visso Omori superposition matches the final day to ratio 1.00, and the run-up rate decays monotonically into Norcia, Spearman rho -1.000), and the spatial b-field is unresolved at both subsample sizes -- a powered FTLS null on an 894k-event Mc 0.20 catalogue, completing the b-value channel at three-for-three], and a twenty-first b-value FTLS test [2009 L'Aquila Mw6.3, the canonical NATURAL foreshock case (basis of the 2012 seismology trial), not a Gulia and Wiemer showcase: a sparse aftershock-dominated catalogue gave an unresolved low foreshock b-positive (0.90), but the foreshock-specific template-matched Cabrera et al. (2022) catalogue (10x denser, Mc 0.80) shows the foreshock b-positive is normal in every phase (1.0-1.1, no drop, 1.01 with the FS1 aftershock burst removed), the prospective b is flat (non-overlapping moving rho 0.015 p 0.937), the rate is a chain of triggered Omori bursts with an overall decay rather than smooth acceleration, and the foreshock b-field has no low-b nucleation asperity (resolved at K=80 with the nucleation patch at the field median) -- denser data converting a sparse false positive to a clean null, completing the b-value channel at four-for-four and extending it to the most-cited natural foreshock case], and a twenty-second b-value/rate FTLS test [2014 Iquique Mw8.1, the canonical accelerated-nucleation subduction megathrust: on the open Sippl et al. (2018) IPOC catalogue (source-box pre-mainshock Mc 2.60) the foreshock b-positive (0.60) is not anomalously low (the Aki 0.44 drop is incompleteness, robust to FS-exclusion; the marginal foreshock-below-aftershock gap at clean Mc is the small Schurr 2014 multi-year decline, not an FTLS RED), the prospective b is flat-to-rising, the acute-window seismicity rate decays with no acceleration excess over an ETAS-lite Omori superposition (final-days ratio 1.10, p 0.28), and the foreshock b-field has no resolved low-b asperity -- so the short-term FTLS b/rate SEISMICITY channel does not capture this nucleation, whose documented precursors (slow slip, migration, the Kato 2016 ~270-day up-dip acceleration, the multi-year b-decline) are aseismic/long-timescale/up-dip and at or below open resolution; fifth case on the channel and the first subduction megathrust])

The remaining unsolved problem is **nucleation of independent mainshocks**, and that information cannot be in the M3.5+ catalogue — it discards >99% of the waveform record, while the candidate precursors (Mc<2 micro-foreshocks, tremor, slow slip) live below catalogue completeness. New approach: build Mc≈1-2 micro-earthquake catalogues directly from continuous raw waveforms with deep-learning phase pickers (SeisBench PhaseNet + PyOcto association, Kaggle GPU), and test whether documented foreshock acceleration/migration is detectable prospectively.

- **Pipeline validated on Iquique 2014** (public GEOFON/IPOC data): 17 foreshock days → 4,806 auto-located micro-events; the catalogue reproduces the documented foreshock migration toward the mainshock epicentre (median distance 182 km → 28 km over 9 days, consistent with Kato & Nakagawa 2014).
- **Tohoku 2011 (Hi-net; ground truth = Kato et al. 2012)**: a dedicated research fetch workflow (`fetch-hinet-research.yml`, window-scoped SAC export) feeds the 2011-03-09 M7.3 foreshock → 03-11 M9 window; PhaseNet on real Hi-net SAC spike-detects the M7.3 itself in a smoke window.
- **Getting clean data was an account-contention problem, not a quota one**: the back-half degradation came from the production Hi-net backfill workflow sharing the single NIED account (one concurrent data request, account-global station selection) with the research fetch — a probe re-fetch returned 0/1 segments while a backfill run was live. Re-asserting the station selection per request (shipped earlier) is necessary but not sufficient; temporarily disabling the backfill workflow for the duration of the re-fetch let all 30 re-fetched segments succeed (30/30), filling the void to ~45 min before the mainshock.
- **Prospective result, scored against a pre-registered test (2026-06-10)**: the void-filled full-window micro-catalogue (5,385 SAC over 03-09 00:00 → 03-11 14:00 JST — to ~45 min before the M9 — 49 stations, 10.7K PhaseNet picks, 87 PyOcto-located events) was scored against criteria fixed *before* the clean re-fetch arrived, to avoid post-hoc statistic tuning: C1 rate-excess (M9-proximal seismicity vs extrapolated M7.3 Omori aftershock decay), C2 migration (per-6h-bin median/p10 distance slopes over the final 30 h), C3 proximity (within-50 km fraction in the final 12 h).
- **Verdict (association catalogue - revised by the 2026-06-11 iterations below): C1 PASS, C2 FAIL, C3 FAIL (1 / 3)** — a genuine near-hypocentre rate excess, but not a clean prospective migration-to-mainshock. C1: M9-proximal (≤75 km) events in the final 30 h run **4.75× the rate predicted by extrapolating the M7.3 aftershock decay** (17 observed vs 3.6 predicted) — real elevated foreshock activity around the eventual hypocentre, from raw waveforms with no catalogue input (the Omori fit rests on only 5 proximal events, so the multiplier is approximate, but the excess is qualitatively clear). C2/C3 fail because the final two 6-h bins (03-11 06:00 / 12:00 JST) are sparse (n = 3 / 5) and locate onshore: the robust distance slope over the final 30 h comes out positive, and only 1 of 12 events in the final 12 h falls within 50 km.
- **Why C2/C3 fail, and the next lever**: the bins up to 03-11 00:00 JST *do* approach (median 207 → 78 km, p10 → 33 km), but that is a post-hoc sub-window the pre-registered test deliberately does not credit. The M9 nucleation patch sits ~180 km offshore, at the edge of the onshore Hi-net array's resolving power, and a homogeneous 0-D velocity model breaks down beyond ~200 km (Pn) — so the immediate pre-mainshock events either go undetected or mislocate onshore. Demonstrating clean migration-to-the-mainshock prospectively would need an offshore/1-D velocity model or template/cross-correlation relocation (as Kato et al. 2012 used), not naive association — that is the next lever, not a physical null.
- **Methods iterations (2026-06-11) - the verdict does not improve, and C1 weakens under uniform detection sensitivity.** (1) A layered 1-D NE-Japan velocity model (Moho 33 km + mantle Pn 8.0 km/s, PyOcto travel-time tables) improves mid-window offshore locations (p10 distance 26-35 km; the 03-11 00:00 bin moves to median longitude 142.35E, just short of the hypocentre at 142.86E) but the final 12-18 h stay sparse and mislocated onshore - verdict unchanged (C1 PASS 4.75x, C2/C3 FAIL). (2) A Kato-2012-style matched filter (the 85 located events as 4-s templates, 2-8 Hz bandpass, network-stacked normalized cross-correlation, 9xMAD threshold; 85/85 self-detections, +234 new detections, 319-event catalogue) equalizes detection sensitivity across the whole window - and the pre-registered verdict becomes **C1 FAIL (1.43x), C2 FAIL, C3 FAIL (0 / 3)**. With 38 rather than 5 fit-window proximal events anchoring the Omori extrapolation, the final-30 h excess drops from 4.75x to 1.43x, below the registered 2x threshold. Honest reading: the apparent near-hypocentre rate excess was largely a detection-sensitivity artifact - the M7.3 aftershock zone itself lies within 75 km of the M9 hypocentre, and once sensitivity is uniform the final-30 h proximal rate is consistent with ordinary M7.3 aftershock decay. None of the pre-registered prospective criteria survive the highest-sensitivity catalogue: onshore-only Hi-net data does not prospectively resolve the documented nucleation signals. Resolving them would need offshore instrumentation (OBS; S-net exists only post-2011) or a different case.
- **Case 2 methods (2026-06-12): Kumamoto 2016 — the same prospective test on a fully onshore case.** The Tohoku null's stated boundary condition was array resolution (nucleation patch ~180 km offshore). The 2016 Kumamoto sequence (Mj 6.5 foreshock 2016-04-14 21:26 JST on the northern Hinagu fault → Mj 7.3 mainshock 28 h later at 01:25 JST, hypocentres ~4.5 km apart at 11-12 km depth; ground truth = Kato et al. 2016 GRL: northeastward foreshock migration + slow slip toward the mainshock initiation point) places the entire nucleation zone inside the dense onshore Hi-net array. The research fetch workflow is now station-box-parameterized (lat/lon inputs); the full 50 h window (04-14 00:00 → 04-16 02:00 JST, 20 Kyushu stations, 2,850 SAC, 50/50 segments) was fetched with the production backfill workflow paused (account-contention lesson), and a pre-registered verdict script — C1 Omori rate excess (≤10 km of the mainshock epicentre, fit window placed after the second Mj 6.4 foreshock so its transient inflates the prediction conservatively), C2 Theil-Sen migration (per-2h-bin median and p25 distance), C3 final-6 h proximity fraction (≤5 km, scaled to the 4.5 km foreshock-mainshock separation) — was fixed before any waveform was picked, with the final verdict to be taken on the matched-filter-equalized catalogue per the Tohoku sensitivity-artifact lesson. PhaseNet → PyOcto (1-D) → matched-filter ran as a single 5.4 h Kaggle GPU kernel.
- **Case 2 verdict (2026-06-12, pre-registered, matched-filter catalogue): C1 FAIL (1.11x), C2 FAIL (+0.04 km/h), C3 FAIL (0.498) — 0 / 3, second honest null.** The pipeline itself performed ideally: 19 stations, 50/50 covered hours, 48,699 PhaseNet picks, 1,863 PyOcto-located events, 400/400 matched-filter self-detections, +745 new detections → a 2,608-event detection-uniform micro-catalogue of the 28 h foreshock sequence. Against the pre-registered criteria: C1 — final-12.4 h mainshock-proximal (≤10 km) count is 789 observed vs 711 Omori-extrapolated (1.11x; 1.24x on the plain association catalogue), i.e. the rate near the future initiation point is ordinary combined M6.5+M6.4 aftershock decay; C2 — Theil-Sen slopes of per-2h-bin median/p25 distance are slightly *positive* (+0.042 / +0.016 km/h): the cloud marginally expands rather than approaches; C3 — 220/442 = 0.498 of final-6 h events within 5 km, one event short of the 0.5 threshold (0.71 at the report-only 7.5 km radius). Honest reading: the foreshock cloud straddles the future initiation point from the first hours (median distance 3.5-5 km throughout, vs ~4.5 km foreshock-mainshock separation), so the registered bulk-migration/proximity statistics have little dynamic range here — and what motion there is points away, not toward. The pre-M6.5 background (21 h) shows nothing at the future site (near-fraction 0.0 in every pre-foreshock bin).
